## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: The task seeks a constitutive relationship σ(ε, T) describing how stress depends on strain and temperature, which is central to materials science and solid mechanics. Temperature typically softens materials while strain hardens them, and their coupling can involve thermal activation, phase transitions, or thermoelastic effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (elastic-plastic with hardening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) (exponential saturation of stress with strain)
- Johnson-Cook type (isothermal): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermally-activated flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal softening with hardening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (multiplicative power-law coupling)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (bilinear with cross-term)
- Zener-Hollomon motivated: sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon + 1) * exp(c2 * T) (logarithmic hardening with thermal activation)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/hyperbolic sine creep law)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 + c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal term)
- Polynomial thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with thermal coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening with saturation → logarithmic log(1+ε) or Voce-type (1-exp(-c*ε)) functional forms
- Thermal softening of modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*(T/T_m)**n) or (T_m - T)**c applied to stress
- Thermally-activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(-c/T) multiplying a strain-dependent term
- Multiplicative decomposition → stress = f(ε) * g(T), separable strain hardening and thermal softening
- Yield stress plus hardening → additive form σ = σ_0 + f(ε) where σ_0 may depend on temperature
- Logarithmic strain hardening → log(1 + c*ε) appears in materials with decelerating hardening rate
- Hyperbolic sine stress dependence → sinh(c*σ) or asinh(c*ε) appears in creep and hot deformation models
- Phase transition or anomalous behavior → non-monotonic temperature dependence, e.g., Gaussian or peaked T terms
